## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where the restoring force depends nonlinearly on position x, possibly with velocity-dependent damping and/or time-dependent driving. The equation of motion generalizes the simple harmonic oscillator by adding anharmonic terms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (cubic + damping + harmonic drive)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonic terms)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * Abs(x) (asymmetric nonlinear restoring)
- Pendulum-like (sine restoring): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (exact pendulum restoring force)
- Pendulum with damping and drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Quadratic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping (cubic velocity): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)
- Combined position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v (multiplicative coupling)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect symmetric potential wells
- Even-power terms in position (x**2) break spatial symmetry — indicate asymmetric potentials or shifted equilibria
- Velocity-dependent terms linear in v indicate viscous/linear damping or energy injection
- Products of position powers with velocity (x**2 * v) indicate amplitude-dependent damping characteristic of self-excited oscillators
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) suggest rotational or pendulum-type geometry rather than spring-based systems
- Sinusoidal functions of time cos(c*t) indicate external periodic driving forces
- Sign-preserving nonlinearities like x**3 vs sign-alternating like x**2 distinguish hardening/softening springs from asymmetric forces
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous (conservative or dissipative) system; presence suggests forced oscillation
- If dv_dt depends only on x (no v, no t), the system is conservative with a potential energy function derivable by integration
- Negative coefficient on v term indicates energy dissipation (damping); positive coefficient indicates energy pumping (self-excitation)

GT: -c0*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x**c4
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.752289977167006*v*(1 - x**2) - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Let me expand this:
`-0.752289977167006*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Combining the v terms:
`(-0.752289977167006 - 0.61401597703647)*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

= `-1.366305954203476*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

So the GT has terms: `c*v + c*v*x**2 + c*x**3 + c*v*exp(-|x|)`

The key difficult term is `v*exp(-|x|)`. Let me check candidates that have exponential terms in x multiplied by v.

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*x)` type terms:** 6, 9, 20, 23, 24, 36, 38, 41, 42, 49

For these, the term is `c1*v*exp(c2*x)`. But the GT has `v*exp(-|x|)`, which involves `|x|`, not `x`. Since `exp(-|x|)` ≠ `exp(c*x)` for any constant c (they behave differently for positive vs negative x), these can't match.

**Candidates with `sin` terms:** 3, 7, 42, 48 — sin can't replicate exp(-|x|).

**Candidates with polynomial-only terms in x multiplied by v:** 1, 2, 8, 10, 12, 13, 16, 25, 27, 31, 32, 33, 34, 35, 37, 47 — These lack exp(-|x|), so they can't match.

**Candidates with `v*exp(c*x**2)` terms:** 19, 28, 43, 44 — `exp(c*x**2)` is symmetric in x like `exp(-|x|)`, but `exp(c*x**2)` ≠ `exp(-|x|)` for any c.

**Candidates with `x*|x|` or `|x|` terms:** 6, 11, 21 — These have `x*Abs(x)` terms but not `v*exp(-Abs(x))`.

**Candidates with `v*x**c` (free exponent):** 29, 30, 40, 45, 46, 50

Look at **candidate 50:** `c0*v + c1*v*x**2 + c2 + c3*x**3 + c4*v*x**c5 + c6*v`

This simplifies to `(c0+c6)*v + c1*v*x**2 + c2 + c3*x**3 + c4*v*x**c5`. This has polynomial terms in x times v, plus a power-law term `v*x**c5`. But we need `v*exp(-|x|)`, which is not a power law.

**Candidate 26:** Has `t` terms — GT doesn't depend on t independently, so this could work if the t-terms vanish (set c5=0, c8=0), reducing to candidate 8. But candidate 8 can't match.

**Candidate 4, 5:** Rational function terms — can't replicate exp(-|x|).

After checking all candidates, none of them contain a term that can reproduce `v*exp(-Abs(x))`. The exponential candidates have `exp(c*x)` (not symmetric), the power-law candidates have `x**c` (not exponential), and polynomial candidates obviously can't match. The `exp(c*x**2)` candidates have the wrong functional form as well.

No candidate can match the GT.

[NO MATCH]

Conclusion: No match

We need: v, v·x², v·exp(-x), x³. Setting c2=-1 gives v·exp(-x). But we need a pure v term. There's no standalone v term here. c3 is a constant (not multiplied by v). We can't get the v term.
